  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bf510b40-1980-44fe-b882-b6748f6d2164'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer1577853822916412386"><p>
  <i>Dear Reader,</i>
</p><p>If you have just picked up this book, then it is not too late to put it back down. Like the previous books in A SERIES OF UNFORTUNATE EVENTS, there is nothing to be found in these pages but misery, despair, and discomfort, and you still have time to choose something else to read.</p><p>Within the chapters of this story, Violet, Klaus and Sunny Baudelaire encounter</p></span>
  <span id="freeText1577853822916412386" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>Dear Reader,</i>
</p><p>If you have just picked up this book, then it is not too late to put it back down. Like the previous books in A SERIES OF UNFORTUNATE EVENTS, there is nothing to be found in these pages but misery, despair, and discomfort, and you still have time to choose something else to read.</p><p>Within the chapters of this story, Violet, Klaus and Sunny Baudelaire encounter a darkened staircase, a red herring, some friends in a dire situation, three mysterious initials, a liar with an evil scheme, a secret passageway, and parsley soda.</p><p>I have sworn to write down these tales of the Baudelaire orphans so the general public will know each terrible thing that has happened to them, but if you decide to read something else instead, you will save yourself from a heapful of horror and woe.</p><p>
  <i>With all due respect,</i>
</p><p>Lemony Snicket</p></span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1346116-what-dose-the-table-of-elements-does-not">what dose “the table of elements does not contain one of the most powerful elements that make up our world, and that is the element of surprise”? mean</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1346116'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F172327.The_Ersatz_Elevator">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1346116-what-dose-the-table-of-elements-does-not">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1346116-what-dose-the-table-of-elements-does-not">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7934577-geneva"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1487924461i/7934577._UY100_CR38,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7934577-geneva">Geneva</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It means that a scientific "element" like oxygen is not the same type of "element" as the one in the phrase "the element of surprise." He's describing<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It means that a scientific "element" like oxygen is not the same type of "element" as the one in the phrase "the element of surprise." He's describing the difference between the two uses, because he wants young readers to know this, as he will go on to mention the element of surprise multiple times throughout the book. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div class='flagAnswer'>
<a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link729695" title="Flag this answer as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=729695&amp;resource_type=CommunityAnswer&amp;return_url=%2Fquestions%2F1346116-what-dose-the-table-of-elements-does-not%2Fanswers%2F729695-it-means-that-a">flag</a>
</div>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div id="review_2731015408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2731015408" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2731015408?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=middle-grade-children-s">middle-grade-children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2731015408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer423864869987538564">We took a break after book five again, and it felt great to get back into the series. This installment turned out to be one of our favorites yet.<br/><br/>We begin with the Baudelaires who are now being delivered by Mr. Poe to their new guardians (the Squalors) at 667 Dark Avenue. After meeting Jerome and Esmé Squalor, it seems that everything might finally work out and the children will actually have a safe place to stay in this massive, 71-room penthouse apartment. Jerome Squalor is kind and has sympath</span>
  <span id="freeText423864869987538564" style="display:none">We took a break after book five again, and it felt great to get back into the series. This installment turned out to be one of our favorites yet.<br /><br />We begin with the Baudelaires who are now being delivered by Mr. Poe to their new guardians (the Squalors) at 667 Dark Avenue. After meeting Jerome and Esmé Squalor, it seems that everything might finally work out and the children will actually have a safe place to stay in this massive, 71-room penthouse apartment. Jerome Squalor is kind and has sympathy for the children while Esmé, on the other hand, seems to be a bit strange. The children learn quickly that life on Dark Avenue is all about what's "in" and "out" and luckily, orphans during this time are "in" along with aqueous martinis, pinstripe suits, and parsley soda.<br /><br />The Baudelaires can't help but wonder about the predicament the Quagmires are in. In the last book, the Quagmires risked everything to try to help the Baudelaire children before being whisked away by Count Olaf, the furtune-hunter. He's discovered more treasure and plans to steal the Quagmire sapphires as well. The Baudelaires must find a way to save their friends, but they have to find out where Count Olaf is hiding them first. Where are they, and what does Olaf plan to do with them?<br /><br />This book was really satisfying with a thicker plot, more comedy, new villains, and more action. The narrative is totally unpredictable and just when you think you have it figured out, you realize you don't. The adults that you think might actually help always seem to fall short; the majority (if not all of them) make you shake your head in disbelief. We found it comical at times and perhaps the best aspect is that Count Olaf works in the background throughout much of the narrative while the Baudelaires devise plans to locate their friends and save them, and themselves. It's difficult to figure out what Count Olaf has in store for all of them.<br /><br />I've said in my previous reviews of the books in this series that I love the themes, especially the loving, family relationship the Baudelaires have with each other, which is portrayed even stronger in this installment. They stick together and remain brave throughout everything. It's inspiring and I appreciate their perseverance with the way they stand up for what's right--never giving up--no matter what. It's truly the light in the darkness of these books.<br /><br />Overall, this installment kept us interested from beginning to end. We're looking forward to moving on with book seven.<br /><br />5*****</span>
  <a data-text-id="423864869987538564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1095240562?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1095240562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11987347279334455675">I'm slowly catching up with the reviews on ASoUE. Currently I'm reading book 12 of 13 to Celyn.<br/><br/>The story formula is eroding by book 6 and some welcome variety / twists are introduced.<br/><br/>More surreal adventure, more amusement for the adults in the translation of Sunny's bon mots. More skulduggery from Count Olaf and friends. Very few questions answered and lots more posed.<br/><br/>Whilst the absurdity doesn't scale the heights of Sunny's teeth vs sword duel in book 4 we do get to see Sunny scale the heights </span>
  <span id="freeText11987347279334455675" style="display:none">I'm slowly catching up with the reviews on ASoUE. Currently I'm reading book 12 of 13 to Celyn.<br /><br />The story formula is eroding by book 6 and some welcome variety / twists are introduced.<br /><br />More surreal adventure, more amusement for the adults in the translation of Sunny's bon mots. More skulduggery from Count Olaf and friends. Very few questions answered and lots more posed.<br /><br />Whilst the absurdity doesn't scale the heights of Sunny's teeth vs sword duel in book 4 we do get to see Sunny scale the heights of an 88 story building using just her teeth. We're also treated to schemes designed to make a physicist weep (this one at least) - yes, it's a children's story for fun ... but why not take a moment to make sense? Violet is an inventor - a great role model for the young girls reading. Excellent. But couldn't her inventions contain an ounce of sense?<br /><br />Witness: Invention to burn through the bars of a cage. Welding torches! How are they made? By heating cooking tongs in an oven. <br /><br />i) It's nonsense to say the oven reaches a temperature high enough to melt metal. Even if it did it would melt itself.<br /><br />ii) The tongs would melt.<br /><br />iii) We see the tongs shade as they heat up ... but in the wrong order. They go through yellow and orange before reaching 'red hot' - surely any adult (and most children) know red is the lowest temperature when dealing with glowing metal and white-hot is the hottest. <br /><br />iv) The tongs would cool down during the 88 story descent to the cage.<br /><br />v) The tongs (even if white hot and having a much higher melting point than cage bars) would not hold enough heat to melt the bars - they would simply heat up the bar a bit.<br /><br />Yes, this is science pedantry, but it's also incredibly basic / obvious and Violet would be a far more interesting and compelling role-model if her inventions weren't ... nonsense.<br /><br />Anyway, the story was pretty good, Celyn enjoyed it, and we moved sharply on to book 7.<br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />.....</span>
  <a data-text-id="11987347279334455675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17500005624207446464"><b>
  <i>4.5</i>
</b><br/><br/>OMG OMG THIS KEEPS GETTING BETTER AND BETTER! <br/><br/>I think this may be the best entry to the series as far as the first 6 books are concerned. A lot of revelations were revealed, especially with regards to the Quagmire twins. I knew there was something fishy going on with Esmé Squalor as soon as she was introduced in this book. As for Jerome Squalor...why? Just why would he abandon and give away the Baudelaires? I feel like he would be a really great guardian for them. Oh well, I understand hi</span>
  <span id="freeText17500005624207446464" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>4.5</i>
</b><br /><br />OMG OMG THIS KEEPS GETTING BETTER AND BETTER! <br /><br />I think this may be the best entry to the series as far as the first 6 books are concerned. A lot of revelations were revealed, especially with regards to the Quagmire twins. I knew there was something fishy going on with Esmé Squalor as soon as she was introduced in this book. As for Jerome Squalor...why? Just why would he abandon and give away the Baudelaires? I feel like he would be a really great guardian for them. Oh well, I understand his decisions since he really wanted to protect them..<br /><br />Despite all that, I love seeing the Baudelaires overcome their adversities under the evil, good-for-nothing Count Olaf. Overall, I enjoyed this one the most. I couldn't stop reading until I'm finished with it. There's always a secret waiting to be exposed in this book. Loved it!<br /><br /> Anyway, I decided to take a short break from this series. I'll read maybe a couple of books before I could continue with it again. It was a great journey so far. 'Til we meet again, ASOUE!</span>

<div id="review_499801269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/499801269" />
    <a title="Skeletonized" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13652071-skeletonized"><img alt="Skeletonized" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350311025p2/13652071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/499801269?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skeletonized" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skeletonized" href="/user/show/13652071-skeletonized">Skeletonized</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499801269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1621236720542258812">I'm getting tired and bored of this. Nothing new happens! The same things happen again and again and again and again.... Had it not been for the author's pleasant and playful style I would have threw this out the window. URGH!<br/>Spoilers ahead!<br/>Seriously now. Halfway through I know what is going to happen: the Baulderies will find out a way to stop Count Olaf who will be revealed in the end (with Mr. Poe assisting, appearing from nowhere at all, coming from the mountains in a random place) and manag</span>
  <span id="freeText1621236720542258812" style="display:none">I'm getting tired and bored of this. Nothing new happens! The same things happen again and again and again and again.... Had it not been for the author's pleasant and playful style I would have threw this out the window. URGH!<br />Spoilers ahead!<br />Seriously now. Halfway through I know what is going to happen: the Baulderies will find out a way to stop Count Olaf who will be revealed in the end (with Mr. Poe assisting, appearing from nowhere at all, coming from the mountains in a random place) and managing to escape (THROUGH A FURIOUS CROWD!). <br />Now, now. I am aware of the fact that this book is targeted to a rather... naive public, but seriously now I expect some intriguing action, something to keep me in a stew, left me wonder "What will they do next?".<br />Step 1: find a human sterotype and turn him into a guardian<br />Step 2: make Count Olaf appear in a very random way<br />Step 3: find out his plan<br />Step 4: Reveal him in public<br />Step 5: let Count Olaf escape easily<br />The End.<br />I have to admit that I love Lemony's style.<br />It is indeed simply addictive but it's worth nothing if he can't make some original stories. I mean, the first book was amaizing but having to re-read it 6 times (because basically all the books seem the same) it's simply torture.<br />Now that I've started the series I am going to torture myself until the end (I hope it's worth it!!).<br />Never shall one compare this to the masterpice Harry Potter series. Never.<br /> What I admire most is the idea of "misfortune", that the good characters don't always "win". This is interesting, appealing and all.<br />As a conclusion: I would have better just watched the movie, I hear Jim Carrie is in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1621236720542258812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3117624896777577430"><b>4.4/5</b><br/><br/>I liked this one a lot!<br/>Even if the main plot and development is the same as the previous books, <b>it had a very fun and enjoyable story with some additions and a very cool, even if simple, setting.</b><br/><br/><b>I liked how different the two new guardians are</b>, how Mr Squalor wants to help the children and even if he understands them he has to please at the same time Mrs Squalor.<br/>Her character is absolutely terrible, but in a fun way, she was so focused on what was in and out that was the only thing that matt</span>
  <span id="freeText3117624896777577430" style="display:none"><b>4.4/5</b><br /><br />I liked this one a lot!<br />Even if the main plot and development is the same as the previous books, <b>it had a very fun and enjoyable story with some additions and a very cool, even if simple, setting.</b><br /><br /><b>I liked how different the two new guardians are</b>, how Mr Squalor wants to help the children and even if he understands them he has to please at the same time Mrs Squalor.<br />Her character is absolutely terrible, but in a fun way, she was so focused on what was in and out that was the only thing that mattered to her, seriously, nothing else.<br />As soon as new things were in, she needed them as soon as possible. <br /><b>Count Olaf's disguise here is very cool too</b>, and even if he is not as present as in some other stories, his presence is pretty creepy this time. <br /><br /><b>I liked the whole "almost endless" stairs' and elevators' concept</b> and especially how the elevator was used later.<br />The whole finale was pretty amazing. The main objective of the children is to find their friends and nothing will stop them.<br />It's a fight against time and they will work super hard not to fail.<br /><br />This was a <b>super fun read, finally some mystery was involved too</b>, to give to the series a little shake and a fresh new side story.<br />The kids will be pretty busy next time, I guess!<br /><br />Till the next tragedy ;) <br /></span>

<div id="review_1701701994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701701994" />
    <a title="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond"><img alt="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494279381p2/47129377.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" href="/user/show/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond">Melanie (TBR and Beyond)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701701994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4605538552943715522"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“The children knew, as I'm sure you know, that there is usually no reason to be afraid of the dark, but even if you are not particularly afraid of something, you might not want to get near it” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/>This installment wasn't my favorite but there was still lots to enjoy about it. <br/><br/>The Baudelaire children are back again and as unlucky as usual. This time the Baudelaire's are staying with a couple that is obsessed with anything "in," meaning trendy. This leads to some great satire and some real</span>
  <span id="freeText4605538552943715522" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“The children knew, as I'm sure you know, that there is usually no reason to be afraid of the dark, but even if you are not particularly afraid of something, you might not want to get near it” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br />This installment wasn't my favorite but there was still lots to enjoy about it. <br /><br />The Baudelaire children are back again and as unlucky as usual. This time the Baudelaire's are staying with a couple that is obsessed with anything "in," meaning trendy. This leads to some great satire and some really fun situations. The woman they are staying with is very cold, and shows the children no affection. Her husband, on the other hand, is compassionate towards the children but a complete coward. The Bauderlaire's are still looking for the triplets and watching out for when Count Olaf is going to appear next. <br /><br />I have been loving this series and although this wasn't my favorite, it was still an enjoyable read. I loved the story line about wanting only things that were trendy, including foster children. It is what really made this book to me. The idea of getting foster children but they were trending in that town among the rich is priceless and a little too on the nose. One of my favorite things so far that has be satirized in these books. <br /><br />The kids were endearing as ever and it was nice to see that we are starting to break formula a bit from the same pattern as the first five books. I love that there is a mystery to what in the world V.F.D is and it's most certainly motivating me to read more in the series. It's driving me mad that I can't figure it out! Oh, and who the hack is Beatrice!!!! I must know these answers!<br /><br />You see most of the same regulars show up in this one, yep that means Olaf is back. I like that he is not as front and center as before though. They are starting to focus on different elements, as well as adding more villainous characters to the list. The reason I only gave this one three stars is because I found myself a little bored a few times and having to push through. I think if the book had been just a little shorter, it would have been a better read. I don't have a lot of complaints about it though, it's possible that I just got a bit bored because I read six of these in a row and I needed a break. Either way, I'd still recommend this book if you enjoyed the other in the series. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4605538552943715522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer5999786033222171767">The Ersatz Elevator is the sixth book in the series in which Violet,Klaus and Sunny are standing of 667 dark Avenue which is not far away from their own house.Their new guardians Jerome and Esme Squalor lived in a creepy building where everything was decided according to the trend of 'IN' things. The things that were 'IN' was high in demand and was considered as a show of status and Esme was particular about these sorts of things. As soon as the Baudelaire arrive they first encounter that the el</span>
  <span id="freeText5999786033222171767" style="display:none">The Ersatz Elevator is the sixth book in the series in which Violet,Klaus and Sunny are standing of 667 dark Avenue which is not far away from their own house.Their new guardians Jerome and Esme Squalor lived in a creepy building where everything was decided according to the trend of 'IN' things. The things that were 'IN' was high in demand and was considered as a show of status and Esme was particular about these sorts of things. As soon as the Baudelaire arrive they first encounter that the elevators were out, this means it was out of order as well as out of fashion trend.They climbed all the way up to 88 floors and finally reached the penthouse of their new guardians.The only reason they were allowed to lived in that penthouse was because the trend of 'In' was now extended to adopt orphans. <br /><br /><br /><br />After a series of IN and OUT things episodes, the children were informed the 'IN' auction being organized by Mrs. Squalor and the event will be managed by a man named Guntur who was none other than you know who.<br /><br /><br />Meanwhile we also come to know that Count Olaf has brought the kidnapped Quagmires children along with him.The mystery of V.F.D still remains unsolved as the Baudelaire busied themselves to help the Quagmires escape.This acronym is making me more curious and i think it is related to the fire which killed their parents.<br /><br /><br />This series just keeps getting better and better,i love it even though the Baudelaire were unsuccessful,they still determined to defeat this perfidious Olaf. It most certainly seems that the addition of new negative characters is significant for the ultimate End Game.While the Baudelaire were yet again disappointed by the inability of their guardians to protect them rather then throwing them off into the line of fire,they come to realize that they need to protect and support each other in order to bring Count Olaf down and stop him from successfully purloining their fortune and the Quagmire Sapphires.</span>

<div id="review_235548335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235548335" />
    <a title="Hayk Mirzoyan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6236870-hayk-mirzoyan"><img alt="Hayk Mirzoyan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315538424p2/6236870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235548335?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hayk Mirzoyan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hayk Mirzoyan" href="/user/show/6236870-hayk-mirzoyan">Hayk Mirzoyan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235548335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13566965906320590082">The book "The Ersatz Elevator" is a book I chose to read, because it looked interesting and I thought the title would lead to an interesting story. In this book, three orphans named Violet, Klaus and Sunny(whose parents were killed in a fire), had to live with the Squalors, and soon, a evil man named Olaf who had been chasing them for their enormous fortune, caught up with them. The three kids had to avoid his nasty clutches, and also rescue their two friends who got captured by Olaf, in the fif</span>
  <span id="freeText13566965906320590082" style="display:none">The book "The Ersatz Elevator" is a book I chose to read, because it looked interesting and I thought the title would lead to an interesting story. In this book, three orphans named Violet, Klaus and Sunny(whose parents were killed in a fire), had to live with the Squalors, and soon, a evil man named Olaf who had been chasing them for their enormous fortune, caught up with them. The three kids had to avoid his nasty clutches, and also rescue their two friends who got captured by Olaf, in the fifth book. My favorite quote in the book was; "Sometimes, when all seems unclear, the answer should be in front of your nose." This was my favorite quote because it taught me, that, even if something looks hard and unsolvable, if tried to solve, can be solved. My interpretation was that something hard can actually be easy, if tested.<br /><br />I also thought that the author's style was interesting, and weird. The author would always say something complex, then explain it! He would even define tricky vocabulary! I thought this style was interesting because it is rare and educational. The author's point of view was third person and I hated it! I would never understand any of the character's feelings. Also, I got really sleepy after a while of reading third person. Finally, I would recommend this book to anyone. I think this book teaches great lessons, and stresses the meaning of life. However, I would probably recommend this most to young adults, because this isn't the kind of book I think many young adults read. It teaches vocabulary, and the meaning of life. Overall I would give this book 3/5 stars. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13566965906320590082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U911p4ExJ7woIcjJ3oWsCCvasWDe5CXn/7/Rd4/eL0rh6W2a451Igi9vm6MxZqub/7kQEArv7iQqOieRJfRNig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3Bb0DolaPdkDTAVUoKNTn04DRRAj8jt4+wbnp4G+4x9uIuwz6/ZS5wQCVj5PQFQMmmDkYPf58LsugxFBK5SB3w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1168344-the-ersatz-elevator">Quotes from The Ersatz Elevator</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;If we wait until we're ready, we'll be waiting for the rest of our lives.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/549633-if-we-wait-until-we-re-ready-we-ll-be-waiting-for">673 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;One of the greatest myths in the world - &amp; the phrase 'greatest myths' is just a fancy way of saying 'big fat lies' -- is that troublesome things get less &amp; less troublesome if you do them more &amp; more. People say this myth when they are teaching children to ride bicycles, for instance, as though falling off a bicycle &amp; skinning your knee is less troublesome the fourteenth time you do it than it is the first time. The truth is that troublesome things tend to remain troublesome no matter how many times you do them, &amp; that you should avoid doing them unless they are absolutely urgent.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/11121-one-of-the-greatest-myths-in-the-world--">496 likes</a>
            </nobr>
